Subject: [sfraves] BSP:  Three Parties. Two Locations. One Weekend....

Content-Type: text/plain; charset=us-ascii

The city may seem really quiet right now but it's not going to stay that way! Just cause so many 
people went to the playa doesn't mean we aren't going to gather to worship the bass!

Thu. Spet. 3rd

BEAT CHURCH?
Shine Mission @ 9th
10pm-2am free

very
happy to be stepping in for my friends Neptune and Kitty-D to bring you
a few of my favorite beat makers.... so come on down enjoy some chilled
beverages in a bar that's not covered in dust! (truly one of the
advantages of staying in the city) 

Metaphor (Addictech)
Cumulous (WoM Sound)
Itteki (Itteki Productions)


Sat Sep. 5th

"Map Point"
Shine Mission @ 9th
10pm-2am free

and 

Toxic Burn II
location tba
1:30am-???? free

of
course i wanted to be there but to be honest i'm glad that i'm not
scrambling for cover to avoid burning in the hot daytime sun, choking
on playa stirred up by dust storms... yeah, it might get a little hot
and sweaty on the dancefloor but that's the way it's supposed to be!

not
that we're gonna spend the entire night all clean and pretty and
indoors. we will dance under the recently full moon kicking up a little
toxic dust of our own, and we will gladly greet the burning brightness
of the morning sun!

some come convene at shine, conveniently
close to bart, have a couple drinks dance to some choice beats and find
out where the party will wind up next. we won't have art cars but
hopefully some caravan can be conjured up to transport us to the next
beat!

Mino (Ambient Mafia)
Harken (Ambient Mafia)
Niles (mk2systems.com)

Jordan Quintaro
Pinkko
Pym
Mr. Rise
Space Invader
Spektrum

for
those of you in the east bay, don't fret there are ways to get around
the bridge being closed! if you feel like it you can drive south to the
san mateo bridge and take 101 north into the city or drive north to the
richmond bridge and then come into the city over the golden gate. if
that seems like too far out of your way to drive, take bart into the
city! after midnight bart will be running limited service all night,
departing the city from powell st or the embarcadero. 

and you thought you'd be stranded....

it
is possible to get to the after party location by bus but i will be
starting a ride share thread here so hopefully we can pack everyone
into cars at shine and caravan there! much more fun than waiting for
the bus and assures that you won't miss a beat on the dancefloor! so
please, everyone! carpool!

one more thing before you rush off to
figure out how you're getting there and what you're going to wear
(saturday be prepared for a fine san francisco morning, which of course
means a chance of fog)

when going to the afterparty be discreet!
do not park at the location, please! there is ample street parking
within a couple blocks of the location on side streets so as not to
draw the attention of the authorities. 

if you see a cruiser going by as you approach the party keep walking until it passes and then double back! 

please take your trash with you when you leave! the less trace we leave the better!

if you know the location of the afterparty please don't post it online! if you must email or call your friends with the info.

if you don't know the location of the afterparty ask around at shine. we'll get you there!

see you on the dancefloor!

peace love and beats - pufuchu


      
--0-1345803975-1251866830=:61289--

[ K O N T R O L ]

minimal techno + avant house
every 1st Saturday at The Endup


featuring from Geneva, Switzerland:

AGN=C8S - LIVE!
http://www.myspace.com/agnesprod
(STHLMaudio . Resopal . Minibar . Perspectiv . Leena . Plak)

Swiss born Agn=E8s has produced for a host of respected labels
in recent years, also finding time to release quality music on
his own label, STHLMaudio. While he first caught the world's
attention with the dubby, minimal tech-house he was crafting a
couple years ago, these days he's been reconnecting with his
deep house roots in a unique way that dancefloors can't resist.


and from Berlin, Germany:

JAN KRUEGER
http://www.myspace.com/jankrueger
(Hello?Repeat . Moon Harbour . Panoramabar)

Jan Krueger is a resident at top Berlin clubs Panoramabar and
Watergate, and the man behind the on point Hello?Repeat
label, home to Daze Maxim, Bruno Pronsato, Cabanne, Audio
Werner and more.  After headlining our January show, Jan so
impressed us that when we heard he was back in the States
this month, we knew we had to invite him back for an encore!


plus special guest:

KENNETH SCOTT
http://www.myspace.com/eutactic
(Moniker . Auralism . Nightlight . Binary)

Kenneth Scott has been a busy boy in the last few years.
In addition to hosting his monthly Binary events and DJing
all over the city, he's also spent much time in the studio,
producing for local labels Auralism, Nightlight, and Blipswitch,
as well as producing and performing live with Emilio "EO"
Orlandi as Moniker, and Jason Short as Eutactic.

AGN=C8S

Agn=E8s is known for his usual deep, dubbed-out minimal techno
productions, but frequently explores more house-influenced rhythms and
textures as well. Agn=E8s runs the Geneva-based label Sthlmaudio
Recordings. Launched in 2003, Sthlmaudio has released tracks by Agn=E8s,
Ripperton, Alessandro Crimi, Chaton, Cabanne, Baaz, Azuni, Skat, and
Luka & Lazo to name a few. In 2007 he released his debut album
=93Dumbles Debuts=94 on Resopal Schallware and has well received EPs on
labels like Minibar, Plak Records, Einmaleins Musik, Perspectiv
Records, Leena and LoMidhigh. Releases under his aliases Ray Valioso
and Cavalier on Deep Vibes, Drumpoet Community and Real Soon only
increased his reputation.  With live and DJ sets, played around the
globe, the clever Swiss producer is taking your dancing requests more
than seriously.  With his now established very personal sound
definition and always grooving, evolving modern beat structures you
can expect a mind-blowing experience.

Below is the official Agn=E8s biography as of mid 2009:

Agn=E8s always dreamed about being a musician. A Jazz drummer for
example, being scheduled in White Horse for two weeks and the next two
in Mourmansk or elsewhere where people are just real. But he's not.
He's just a farmer out of nowhere able to handle computers. The
redneck understood bits and bytes well beyond everybody's believes and
bets... So what do you want to expect from that kind of guy? Honesty,
straight forward thinking and sympathy. If this is what you want, ask
for him, if you need the usual hypocrisy and fake ass shit, pass your
way. There's plenty of those doing that far better then him.

__________________________________________________________


JAN KRUEGER

It's 1995 in D=FCsseldorf - Jan's hometown - and he's consumed by the
Music of Labels like M-Plant, Relief, Sound Signature, Planet E and
Phono. Jan owes his first steps to present his record selection (to
those other than his lovely dog and cat) to a very good friend who
holds a residency at one of the best underground clubs for electronic
music, an old wine cellar located in Wuppertal, near D=FCsseldorf. Here
he had the pleasure to play alongside artists who had inspired him
since the early nineties. In short - this is the precise starting
point of a never ending story fuelled by love for the music.

In 1996, Jan started to work for a record store and focused on hosting
his own parties starring international guests like Daniel Bell,
Matthew Herbert, Ata and Steve Bug. Around the same time, he met the
young and promising producer Daze Maxim. Both clicked right away and
found out that they have a quite similar interest in electronic music.
Both decided to start some excursions in Maxim's backroom studio to
produce deep and minimal house tracks, which were finally released on
Matthias Tanzmann's Moon Harbour Recordings in 2001.

Three years later, Jan determined after sleepless nights to move away
from D=FCsseldorf and all his friends in order to start a new chapter in
Hamburg. Because of his long friendship to the staff of Germany's
leading distribution company Word and Sound, it was a logical step to
take on a position as sales manager there. As a consequence of all
this, it wasn't long before he proposed to Daze that they set up a
platform for him and friends to release music. Hello?Repeat was born.

As a DJ, Jan is adept in the late night hours, playing his highly
individual and addictive mixture of deep house, minimal, and techno
with rough edges, always focused on the dance floor. Today Jan lives
in Berlin and holds a residency at Panoramabar and Watergate and plays
considerably abroad to represent the high quality sound of
Hello?Repeat.

KENNETH SCOTT

Kenneth Scott makes small-scale techno with large sonic concerns.
Producing music as Eutactic with Auralism label head Jason Short, as
Moniker with Emilio "EO" Orlandi, and under his own name for friend
Alland Byallo's Nightlight Music, Scott takes cues from early Warp
records, Matthew Dear's acid experimentation as Audion, and
minimal-minded composers like Philip Glass and Arvo Part. The results
eye the "minimal" label with suspicion, combining techy snares,
reptilian synths, and subtle layers of melody into something melodic,
funky, and emotional -- uncategorizable and catchy as hell, just how
Scott likes it.  "I think that trance really ruined melodies and
arpeggios for everyone," he says, "and only now are people a bit more
open to it." Scott was raised in a small, rural Iowa town, where he
nursed an obsession with dance music while exploring its tiny scene.
He learned a bit of every instrument he could get his hands on, while
DJing his first house parties with his father's old turntable, a
portable CD player, and a Radio Shack mixer. Scott's been honing his
craft in the years since, running San Francisco's successful Binary
party, DJing alongside Pan Pot, Lee Curtiss, and Argenis Brito, and
creating music with collaborators Jason Short, Alland Byallo, and
Emilio Orlandi. Now he's ready to open the floodgates. "I want to
create dance-floor friendly, funky, jacking, sonically dexterous,
soulful music," he says. "I want to make a crowd tear up, as well as
pump their fists."

On Mon, Sep 21, 2009 at 06:12:00AM +0000, Holt Sorenson wrote:
>We now have a flash player on our site. If you know how
>to watch Youtube, you know how to listen to KZSU. So
>please tune in to KZSU by listening to 90.1 in the Bay Area or
>pointing your web browser at: http://kzsulive.stanford.edu/
>
>If you're interested in guest appearing on any of our shows
>or having a mix featured contact us using our email addresses
>or our group address: electronicadjs@kzsu.stanford.edu
>
>Eclektronik Groove w/ Holt Sorenson - Mon 9AM-12PM Pacific/US
>--------------------------------------------------------------
>
>This week DJ Zenith will be mixing live as you get your monday
>morning groove on.
>
>DJ Zenith, Stephanie Blair, was born in Washington, DC but grew up
>all over the world. Her childhood included places such as
>southeastern Virginia; Marquette, Michigan; Angeles City,
>Philippines; and Seoul and Taegu, Korea. Music was part of her life
>from an early age. Whether she was taking classical piano lessons;
>singing while her father played twelve string guitar in talent
>shows; singing in choirs; playing roles including lead in musicals;
>or playing tenor saxophone in symphonic bands; or DJing her college
>radio station; Stephanie grew up immersed in music. Stephanie became
>fascinated by the San Francisco dance scene in Washington, DC where
>she returned to after college. Stephanie finally moved to San
>Francisco in 2002. Stephanie's mixes are characterized by a dominant
>bass line. Fascinated by rhythms, many of her tracks also feature a
>heavy percussion element. Whether she's dropping acid tracks, tracks
>with beautiful female vocals, jazzy tracks, or even hip house
>tracks... she always serves it up with a large side of funk.
>Stephanie has played as close as Black Rock City and as far away as
>Paris. DJ Highlights this year for Stephanie include DJing with
>Green Gorilla Lounge at Burning Man and at Burning Man Camp
>Fundraisers, playing in her home town Washington, DC at the Dragon
>Fly Bar and finally playing in Paris, France at the Lizard Lounge.
>Stephanie is a resident Thursday nights at Sugar with Native
>Intellgence ( Sleevin Records ) and DJ Robb Crush ( Stompy ) as well
>as the Art & Music Sessions on Saturdays with Cez featuring art work
>by Danyol. Stephanie can also be found DJing around San Francisco
>and coming to a warehouse near you.
>
>More about DJ Zenith:
>http://hsomusic.com/sh/o
>http://hsomusic.com/sh/n
>
>You can listen and find out more about Holt's show at:
>http://hsomusic.com/show
>
>Big Love Show with Jack - Mon 3PM-6PM Pacific/US
>------------------------------------------------
>
>This week Jack will be hosting Hector Moralez and Brian Learner.
>
>Hector Moralez
>
>It is very rare that you find an artist like Hector Moralez with such
>love and passion for the music, As one half of the world renowned
>House music producing duo know as Fries & Bridges this
>DJ/Producer/Remixer has made a definite mark over the last 8 years.
>His first release with Phil Weeks "Time to Yourself" on Robsoul
>Recordings gained him acclaim from many artists. Considering this
>was his first release the track made it to many charts in England
>and America. The track was powerful making it on to a live mix CD by
>John Marsh of the Beloved for London's Fabric night club. His
>releases since have come out on some of the worlds best known
>Housemusic imprints.He currently divides his time in the Studio
>between projects with Phil Weeks, Chris Carrier & Block Committee.
>with Original music coming out in the future on his found label
>"Minority Music" traveling back & forth from Paris to Oakland, his
>home for many years.
>
>More about Hector:
>http://hsomusic.com/sh/5n
>
>You can find out more about Jack and his show at:
>http://www.thebigloveshow.com/                                         
>
>Epiphany of Sound with J.C. - Th 9AM-12PM Pacific/US
>----------------------------------------------------
>
>After 14 years, DJ J.C.'s techno/house/electronica showcase has
>garnered much attention and devotion. Like most folks at Stanford's
>radio station, he's a volunteer, proving that his motivation isn't
>a paycheck; it's his passion to share his interest in one of music's
>most eclectic genres. With his conversational style, inclusion of
>producers and musicians from both the local & international scene,
>and his stewardship of the station's 24-hour marathons during
>Solstices and Equinoxes, it's no wonder that DJ J.C has made a
>connection with listeners in a very crowded market. Catch his live
>broadcasts or listen to the previous week's program at underheard.org.
>
>J.C. will email this week if he has an update on any guests.
>Thanks for your support!!!

>
>This week DJ Zenith will be mixing live as you get your monday
>morning groove on.
>
>DJ Zenith, Stephanie Blair, was born in Washington, DC but grew up
>all over the world. Her childhood included places such as
>southeastern Virginia; Marquette, Michigan; Angeles City,
>Philippines; and Seoul and Taegu, Korea. Music was part of her life
>from an early age. Whether she was taking classical piano lessons;
>singing while her father played twelve string guitar in talent
>shows; singing in choirs; playing roles including lead in musicals;
>or playing tenor saxophone in symphonic bands; or DJing her college
>radio station; Stephanie grew up immersed in music. Stephanie became
>fascinated by the San Francisco dance scene in Washington, DC where
>she returned to after college. Stephanie finally moved to San
>Francisco in 2002. Stephanie's mixes are characterized by a dominant
>bass line. Fascinated by rhythms, many of her tracks also feature a
>heavy percussion element. Whether she's dropping acid tracks, tracks
>with beautiful female vocals, jazzy tracks, or even hip house
>tracks... she always serves it up with a large side of funk.
>Stephanie has played as close as Black Rock City and as far away as
>Paris. DJ Highlights this year for Stephanie include DJing with
>Green Gorilla Lounge at Burning Man and at Burning Man Camp
>Fundraisers, playing in her home town Washington, DC at the Dragon
>Fly Bar and finally playing in Paris, France at the Lizard Lounge.
>Stephanie is a resident Thursday nights at Sugar with Native
>Intellgence ( Sleevin Records ) and DJ Robb Crush ( Stompy ) as well
>as the Art & Music Sessions on Saturdays with Cez featuring art work
>by Danyol. Stephanie can also be found DJing around San Francisco
>and coming to a warehouse near you.

>Hector Moralez
>
>It is very rare that you find an artist like Hector Moralez with such
>love and passion for the music, As one half of the world renowned
>House music producing duo know as Fries & Bridges this
>DJ/Producer/Remixer has made a definite mark over the last 8 years.
>His first release with Phil Weeks "Time to Yourself" on Robsoul
>Recordings gained him acclaim from many artists. Considering this
>was his first release the track made it to many charts in England
>and America. The track was powerful making it on to a live mix CD by
>John Marsh of the Beloved for London's Fabric night club. His
>releases since have come out on some of the worlds best known

Subject: [sfraves] BSP:  Pronoia 5-year with Hatiras, this Friday!

$8 presales available here (until midnight tonight!)
https://sanfrancisco.going.com/event-660380;Pronoia_pres_HATIRAS_5-Year_Anniv_Libra_Bash?type=ticketing&step=select

Friday, September 25, 2009
Paradise Lounge
1501 Folsom St.
San Francisco
9:30pm - 4am // 21+

Pronoia turns five this year, and we're celebrating by bringing house
legend / electro-bass bomber HATIRAS back to SF! It's also our annual
Libra birthday bash, with special lower cover for Libras.

DJs delivering huge twisted bass & beats on two sound systems:

(ROOM 1)
HATIRAS (Hatrax | Blow Media - Toronto)
Fresh off a mind-blowing run playing Root Society at Burning Man '09, Hatiras is bringing his unparallelled brand of rocking electro house to SF for a 2 hour set Sept 25. His tracks in the past 2 years (Poppin Beats, Get
Blahsted, and Autograph to name a few) have taken DJ sets to the next
level even when you thought it couldn't get any better! He's a mad
genius who's created classic house tracks (Spaced Invader, anyone?) but
has the pulse of the current scene as solid as anyone out there right
now. With over 100 releases of mindbending, ass shaking music, he's won
2 Juno Awards, a Socan Award for most radio play in Canada and multiple
nominations, owns and operates 2 record labels (Hatrax and Blow Media),
and has sold over half million records worldwide. Everyone from The
Chemical Brothers to Pete Tong to Roger Sanchez, Bad Boy Bill, DJ Dan,
Danny Tenaglia and in between, plays Hatiras music.

+

FELIX THE DOG (Groundscore)
AARON JAE (Evil Breaks | C.O.N.)
RAYDEUS (Pronioa | raydeus.com | jungoroad.com)
REDSTICKMAN (FnF)

+

Visuals by THUNDERGROUND

(ROOM 2)
DEX STAKKER (Opel | Opulent Temple | Pronoia)
P-DUB (GuerillaBASS)
JANA D (Acid Totem)
PIETER RIZEN (Pronoia)

+

sound reinforcement by STRATEGIK


$10 before midnight
$15 after midnight

** $5 off cover for Libras **

Thanks Ray.

I'm not sure if i've ever met you before but allow me to introduce myself.
My name is jay and my buddies and I are attempting to throw a new type of
party where the attendees vote on all the music they want heard the night of
the event via a ballot online. Our first party "way back when" is geared
towards the old schoolers and home base'rs of the day. All the hit's from
the 90's and up and nothing is excluded.

So yea, you and other add music to a ballot and everyone votes on thier
favorite songs and the top 8hrs of music will be played the night of the
event. So far there is some pretty rad music and some tunes i never knew the
name of but i hard many moons ago.(bumchen song to be exact)

The party is in SF. Hope it's your kinda thing and maybe i'll meet ya mug to
mug.

cheers.
(sorry again for jacking your thread. I'm goign to start my own now.)

myself, or Jackie-O, or... brings you?  DOUBTFUL!)  And we simply hope
to bring you the same level of "fuck yeah" that your local Mackie jock
brings you on any given weekend.  So simply put, make sure that you
have the proper (Peter approved) footwear on hand as well as the
non-selfish attitude in mind and then simply tear up whatever surface
it is that you're standing on.  Because the beats have no boundries
and the beats make no judgement.  They simply want you to get out of
your head.

As such, I hope you have the chance to get out of your head more than
you think you need to.  For that is the music, and that is life.

Now dance, MF, dance.

(yay cliches!).

So I don't know what I think of this Dance Democracy idea...but at least it is an innovation of sorts.  

I can see a lot of ways for it to go wrong (try searching for "the stupidity of crowds") but at least it is something new.  I created Live365.com which is a similar kind of idea in a way.  But we worked at the level of mixes or stations rather than individual tracks as you are doing here.  And also we had (when I was there) 40,000 stations to choose from, not just one.

Probably if this was done as input to a live DJ mixing who could select or reject the requests before hand it could be interesting.  I still think there is some value in the live interaction with the audience and the story telling or journey that still has to come from a live DJ.  You also need to constrain the musical requests somehow I think, see http://www.wired.com/culture/design/magazine/17-03/dp_intro

And then there is the value of a DJ who plays something you've never heard before and it seems that the democratic approach will miss a lot of that.  There is an art to playing something weird and out of place that totally works right then and it's not as simple as just mining other people's play lists al a Pandora.

But there's not so much innovation in the scene anymore and what little there is seems to get channeled to the playa...so I am rooting for you guys even if it might not be my cup of tea.

Peter


---------------------------------------------------------------------
To unsubscribe, e-mail: sfraves-unsubscribe@hyperreal.org
For additional commands, e-mail: sfraves-help@hyperreal.org

ADULTNAPPER

"Adultnapper" is a shadowy figure drawn from the dark reaches of Francis
Harris' imagination. Harris, a philosphy phD drop-out with punk rocker
roots, hails from suburban Las Vegas but has called Brooklyn home for the
past 9 years - a stretch in which he has gone from =93hating dance music,=
=94 to
establishing himself as an underground DJ/Producer with a unique sound and =
a
global audience.

In 2004, having achieved success as a DJ, Label Owner and Event Producer,
Harris turned to the studio, intent on exploring new sonic territory, and
adopting the Adultnapper moniker to represent his efforts. What emerged was
a reaction against the skippy rhythms and repetetive loops that had
dominated the electronic dance music landscape. Instead, Harris took a
sophisticated, song-based approach, characterized by elaborate swung
microrhythms, thick musical baselines, complex arrangements, haunting tonal
melodies and brooding introspective atmospheres - and tastemakers took note=
.
A steady stream of Adultnapper tracks have since appeared on some of the
world's most esteemed labels - Steve Bug's Audiomatique, Frank Lorber's
Nummer, Mr. C's Superfreq, Mule Electronic, Dirt Crew, etc. - and have been
hotly tipped by elite DJs - Loco Dice, Danny Tenaglia, Craig Richards, Sven
Vath, Laurent Garnier, Sasha, Monika Kruse, Steve Lawler, Danny Howells,
etc. - thus firmly establishing Harris as one rare purveyor who steadfastly
challenges the conventional wisdom and accepted shortcuts of post modern
electronic music.

In 2007, seeking a platform on which to further develop the Adultnapper
persona, Harris launched Ransom Note, a concept label with a cohesive
narrative that unfolds with each release. Much like a graphic novel, using
text, the =93ransom note,=94 and imagery, a series of drawings by performan=
ce
artist John Stroud, the label's jackets will tell the story of this
anti-hero who is part creative genius gone awry, part tortured dystopic
philospher, part paranoid vigilante outlaw.

Still, it is when Harris himself is in control of a dancefloor that
Adultnapper is truly brought to life. Relying primarily on the ancient art
of mixing two records, Harris' precision skills and thoughtful programming
have earned him a reputation as DJ equal to his regard as producer - an
uncommom distinction. On the decks, Harris intricately weaves divergent
strains into a thick, pumping groove that subtly rises and falls, drawing
the crowd ever deeper within his emotion-laden, melodic journey. Circo Loco
at DC10, Ibiza, Cielo in NY, The End, Mulletover in London, Weekend in
Berlin, Pawn Shop in Miami, Avalon in LA, are just a few of the world's
discenring floors that have been graced by Adultnapper and been left
clamoring for more.

THREE

Three has quietly and steadily earned the respect of his peers the world
over through a handful of truly unique productions and a signature DJing
sound spanning through all things house, techno and beyond. This sound, a
strong knowledge of tradition capped by a fondness for the cutting edge,
continually puts him through a variety of tour dates that show not only
diversity in audience, but a genre-bending passion for good music. A long
time fixture of Florida's legendary Simon's and a former resident at Twilo
in N.Y.C., guest spots have seen him through San Franciso's notorious Wicke=
d
Crew party, London's Fabric, Bedrock, KISS FM , and off-shore to Mexico,
Peru, Costa Rica, Pacha in Buenos Aires and South Africa.

Echoing his wide tastes as a DJ, the unique sound of his productions has
captured a not-so-common cross section of DJ's ears from deep house to
techno, and all things in bewteen.

PEZZNER

Up until 2008 Dave Pezzner was virtually unknown to the electronic dance
music community, aside from his works in the duo =93Jacob London=94 (Classi=
c
Music, Doubledown, U-Freqs). For 16 years he cut his chops with partner Bob
Hansen, creating eccentric house and break beat rhythms often crossing the
lines between bad-ass, funky and hilarious.

In the winter of 2008, Pezzner took to his own studio to begin work on his
first solo output composing songs that are more serious, with an abstract
artistic sensibility. Quickly Dave=92s catalog began to materialize with a
signature sound: Lofty percussive themes with intentions to create hypnotic
soundscapes for the body as well as the brain.

It wasn=92t long before Pezzner found his first 5 songs scooped up by
London-based Freerange Records, covering the first two EP=92s of his career=
,
=93Other Lover=94 and the epic three-part masterpiece =93Almost Here.=94 Th=
ese two
EPs garnered him massive support from artists as varied as John Digweed,
Laurent Garnier, Peter Kruder, Steve Bug and Ben Watt, setting up Pezzner a=
s
a producer on the rise.

These first two releases laid a solid foundation for his career and
follow-ups are now in the pipeline on San Francisco's Om Records imprint,
London=92s Urbantorque Recordings, plus another EP for Freerange. Dave has
also got an arsenal of remixes forthcoming for heavyweights including Josh
Wink, Mark Farina, and Mike Monday. Its a dizzying number of releases for a=
n
emerging artist, but now that Pezzner=92s stepped out on his own, he=92s
definitely got a lot to say.

SUTEKH

Seth Horvitz (b. 1973, Los Angeles) is an electronic musician, sound
designer, DJ, piano programmer, and human based in the San Francisco Bay
Area since 1991. Under the name Sutekh, he has released music on dozens of
record labels, including Mille Plateaux (Germany), Soul Jazz (UK), The Leaf
Label (UK), Orthlorng Musork (USA), and his own Context Free Media. While
identified most often as a techno artist, Sutekh is well known for his
innovative and irreverent approach, incorporating a range of influences fro=
m
pigeon funk, dub, and free jazz to experimental noise, musique concr=E8te, =
and
classical minimalism. Sutekh=92s music is full of surprises, frequently
transitioning between the repetitive and chaotic, abrasive and tranquil,
serious and absurd, with an expansive sonic palette consisting of
synthesized sound, field recordings, acoustic instruments, digital
artifacts, and samples that exploit the beauty and unpredictability of the
recording medium itself.

As a remixer, Sutekh has reinterpreted the work of dozens of artists
including Norweigan Grammy Award winning singer-songwriter Hanne Hukkelberg=
,
micro-sound artist Alva Noto (aka Carsten Nicolai), pioneer of conceptual
art Lawrence Weiner, and the eight piece Klezmer ensemble KLEZ-X. In 2006,
the Leaf Label compiled twenty-three of his remixes into a double-disc and
four-LP set entitled =93Born Again,=94 described by the BBC as =93gorgeous
minimalism paired to an unstoppable propulsiveness and a brilliant
deployment of texture that=92s so tactile it prompts feelings of
synaesthesia.=94

As a live performer, Sutekh has appeared at festivals, museums, concert
halls, and nightclubs around the world, including Mutek (Montreal), Son=E1r
(Barcelona), Dis-patch (Belgrade), Elektrodienos (Vilnius), Croma
(Tenerife), Numero-Projecta (Lisbon), C-Sides (Jerusalem), Bios (Athens),
Sonic Acts (Amsterdam), the San Francisco Electronic Music Festival, Yerba
Buena Center for the Arts (San Francisco), SFMOMA, Cleveland Center for
Contemporary Art, Sydney Opera House, Womb (Tokyo), and Tresor (Berlin).

Horvitz has been an active member of the Bay Area electronic music scene
since the early 1990s. He made his foray into music by conducting a weekly
radio show at KALX Berkeley, deejaying at numerous renegade parties, and
organizing several weekly and one-off club events. Over the years, he has
collaborated with many fellow Bay Area musicians including Joshua Kit
Clayton, Matthew =93Safety Scissors=94 Curry, Matmos, Wobbly, Kevin Blechdo=
m,
and Twerk. He is also a member of the =93band=94 Pigeon Funk, which has rel=
eased
two full length albums on Proptronix (USA) and Musique Risqu=E9e (Canada).

While his musical skills are largely self-taught, Horvitz has taken
coursework in Computer Music and Psychoacoustics at CNMAT (Center for New
Music and Audio Technologies) and studied tabla in India in 1994 while
earning his bachelor=92s degree in Cognitive Science at the University of
California, Berkeley. During the last several years, he has gravitated
towards a more studied approach to composition, taking private lessons in
piano performance and music theory, and completing scores for several
independent films. Currently, he is pursuing an MFA in Composition and
Electronic Music at Mills College in Oakland, California.

Well, I've never been one for those epic stories of how the night went, but:


WOW... WOW...

Seriously, amazing night.  Robert Hood's set was just awesome, banging hard
old detroit style minimal.  His monitor started to cut out in the heat until
some quick work by Pascal fixed that, but he still kept it going hard
through that.  The hard techno and minimal heads all seemed to enjoy it, the
more modern tech-house and berlin style minimal heads found it a bit hard I
think.  The lineup was really well constructed, too.  leadup DJ styles were
different but led naturally into Robert's, and the Fingermonsters sound
followed well, not sounding like some poor attempt to emulate.  I did miss
parts of everyone else's checking out the chill oom, esp Time Slips By, who
were pretty cool.

The night actually seemed to go by pretty fast, come to think of it.  Then
all of a sudden it was coming up on 6am and I was beat. :)

Hopefully the recordings worked out and will be available for download. :)

Subject: Re: [sfraves] ASR roll call...

Hi All,

Kind of sick myself right now and not a lot of energy for review writing....

Party was good but not great IMO.  Good music, top notch sound, minimal but good lighting and decoration.  Cool visuals on the four sided cube thingee.  But somewhat weak vibe.

I'm not a core techno head of course, but I enjoy techno.  However Mr. Hood failed to hold my attention.  Why?  I don't know...

As some may know, I'm a stickler for the vibe, that intangible elusive feeling that you get at a great party as opposed to the merely average.  And the vibe was missing here for me.

About 2/3 into his set we wandered into the chill room and stayed there.  It wasn't just his music, but a lot of things that contributed.  First of all, this party was somewhat of a techno sausage fest.  Not too many girls you know?  I was there with my wife, but a little sexual energy helps to get the dance floor jumping.  That was not happening here...

Also there was this one girl who had taken too much of something, I'm guessing GHB?  I don't know who this person was but if you do or if "too much GHB Asian girl" is on the list, Girl you need to stop taking that shit.  Dry humping random dudes while you fall down is really not attractive and FWIW GHB killed a friend of ours not too long ago...

Meanwhile, the chill area was awesome.  First of all it was actually "chill" as in cooler in temperature than the main room which if you have been to this venue previously tends to heat up fast even if there isn't a huge crowd in there.  I liked that blower thing up front that pumped out the huge volume of cold air.  A really eclectic variety of music was played here a lot of it danceable.  Met several cool people over there too and despite the volume the sound was clean enough to have a conversation.  Heard Andy W's downtempo set and Time Slips By which were both great.  Chill room done right.

I should say again the sound was excellent in both rooms, good job there.

I was somewhat sad that the vending machines had been moved, not sure why.  But the lighting in the bathroom hall area seemed less harsh with them gone and didn't make everyone look like undead zombies while waiting for their friends outside the bathrooms.  We never went upstairs to the bar area...

Saw AndyW, Ray, ChuckG, Adriana, Johnathan Ben Ari, Osby, Terry E., met new friend Amy B and her fiance, and probably someone I am forgetting.  Good to see everyone as always!

Best,

Peter

traced to a conversation I had with a guy (I think it was Matt
Ganucheau) at robotspeak recommending I join sfraves. Eventually I
